⏺ All executable items complete. Stopping at the merge gate — that's the human's
  vertex-A signature.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  The Edit tool didn't fire the no-LaunchAgent reminder hook here (compare to Write
  earlier). That's because the rendered hook block only matches "matcher": "Write",
  not the Edit tool — even though both modify files. This is actually a second
  manifestation of the same Domain E bug: the no-LaunchAgent rule wants to fire on
  file-creation that could land a plist anywhere, but the unconditional Write matcher
   only catches the Write tool. A Bash heredoc to /tmp/foo.plist would bypass it
  entirely. Surgical fix when Domain E gets a dedicated session: not just add if
  clauses, but also expand the matcher to cover Edit + Bash file-creation patterns.
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

⏺ The Compaction Protocol                                                        
                                                                                     
  Short answer: the compaction summary is embedded into the same session JSONL as a  
  single "type":"summary" record — it is not a separate artifact, but it does become 
  the canonical "head" of the JSONL after the event. The full pre-compact turns      
  remain on disk in the same JSONL above that summary record.

  864dae3b52.jsonl                                                                   
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                           
  Evidence: Size after /compact                                                      
  Result: 866K, 296 lines                                                            
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                        
  Evidence: Summary records inside                                                   
  Result: 1 (grep "type":"summary" → 1 match)                                        
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                        
  Evidence: Sibling artifact (e.g. …compact.md)                                      
  Result: None — only <uuid>.jsonl (and some newer-format <uuid>/ directories for 
    multi-file sessions)                                                             
                                                                                     
  So this session has the full pre-compact transcript on disk plus the compact       
  summary, both inside one file. No separate "compaction artifact" was written.      
                                                                                     
  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────                                    
  - Compaction is a context-window operation, not a storage operation. The JSONL on
  disk is append-only — /compact writes a summary record into it but doesn't truncate
   prior turns. What changes is which records get replayed into Claude's context on  
  the next turn: post-compact, only the summary + new turns are loaded; the older    
  verbatim turns are skipped over (still on disk, just not in working memory).   
  - Resume reads the live tail, not the archive. claude --resume re-enters at the
  post-compact state because that's the last context configuration written. The  
  pre-compact turns are forensically recoverable (you can jq through the JSONL), but 
  Claude on resume does not see them — only the summary plus anything after it.     
  - Cross-session persistence is a different mechanism entirely. CLAUDE.md (project +
   global), MEMORY.md, and your output style are re-injected from disk every session 
  start, regardless of compaction. That's why the guidance to save                   
  artifact-paths-and-state to project_artifact_*.md matters — those survive
  compactions and session boundaries because they live outside the JSONL.            
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────                      
                                                   
  The decision matrix you actually care about
                                                                                     
  Information type: User prompts + your responses (verbatim)                         
  Survives compact?: ✗ (replaced by summary)                                         
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)                                              
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/<id>.jsonl                              
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                        
  Information type: Compact summary                                               
  Survives compact?: ✓                                                               
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)                                           
  Stored where?: Same JSONL, "type":"summary" record                                 
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                        
  Information type: CLAUDE.md (project + global)                                  
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected)                                                 
  Survives session close?: ✓                                                      
  Stored where?: Repo + ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md                                          
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                           
  Information type: MEMORY.md + memory files                                         
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected)                                                 
  Survives session close?: ✓                                                         
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/memory/
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Output style                                                     
  Survives compact?: ✓
  Survives session close?: ✓                                                         
  Stored where?: Settings                        
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Skill bodies you invoked                                         
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected, capped 5K each / 25K total)
  Survives session close?: ✗ unless re-invoked                                       
  Stored where?: Skill files                     
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Path-scoped CLAUDE.md (nested)                                   
  Survives compact?: ✗
  Survives session close?: n/a                                                       
  Stored where?: Reloaded on matching file read  
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Tool outputs (older / large)                                     
  Survives compact?: ✗
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)                                              
  Stored where?: Same JSONL                      
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Hooks
  Survives compact?: n/a (code, not context)
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/settings.json

  Practical implications for your workflow                                           
   
  Given your audit-heavy, cross-session reconciliation pattern (Stream 1/2/3 today is
   a clean example):                             
                                                                                     
  1. Forensic audit of "what did the prior session actually do?" → read the JSONL,   
  not the summary. The compact summary loses tool-call detail by design. When you
  sent three parallel Explore agents to verify Stream 1/2/3 claims, you were         
  essentially doing what the JSONL already encodes — except the JSONLs across
  sessions aren't auto-cross-referenced. That's a system gap your IRF-PRT-075 ticket
  (57 unprotected memory scopes) and the Domain D chezmoi propagation are slowly
  closing.
  2. Compact loses tool-call provenance. If a future session needs to know which 
  agent verified what, the summary won't carry it. Solution: write project-type      
  memory files for non-trivial verifications before compact, so the claim → evidence
  chain survives.                                                                    
  3. The SessionStart:compact hook you saw fire in this very turn is the system
  reinjecting memory hygiene context after compact — it's not a "compaction occurred"
   notification, it's a re-priming hook that fires on session start and on
  post-compact resume. The two events look identical to a hook because both are      
  "context just got rebuilt."                    
                                      
  Where to look next if you want to dig deeper                                       
   
  - jq 'select(.type=="summary")' <jsonl> — extracts just the compact summary records
   from any session                              
  - jq 'select(.type=="user")' <jsonl> | wc -l — tells you how many human prompts    
  that session had                                                                   
  - The <uuid>/ directory format (vs <uuid>.jsonl) appears in newer sessions — likely
   the sub-agent transcript bundling pattern, where parallel Agent calls each get    
  their own JSONL nested under the parent's directory. Worth a peek if you want to
  audit how your 519 Agent-tool calls were actually serialized.                      
                                                 
  End-of-turn: protocol clarified — compaction is in-JSONL, not a separate artifact, 
  and is a context-replay decision rather than a storage decision. No file changes
  made.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────                                    
  - The cascade is a self-observation loop, not a sequence of tasks. The report
  observes failure modes → governance rules get installed to prevent them →          
  installation itself becomes session data → next report observes whether the
  installation succeeded or reproduced the failure. Other-Claude installing CLAUDE.md
   sections derived from a report it never opened was the loop catching itself: the  
  very rule it was writing ("Verification Before Action") would have prevented the 
  mistake of skipping the URL. The user is demonstrating the loop's diagnostic power
  by showing me the recursion in flight.                                            
  - Cascade durability is multi-layer by design. Memory files (chezmoi-mirrored to
  remote) carry decisions forward; gitignored .txt preservation files keep        
  compaction-summary detail local-only because compactions inherit                   
  privilege-sensitive context; MEMORY.md pointers index the graph. Each layer answers
   a different question: memory = "what was decided," txt preservation = "what was   
  the full reasoning," index = "where to look." If any single layer fails, the others
   reconstitute most of the picture.                                                 
  - session-meta/ is the substrate the report reads. 435 session-meta entries means
  the report isn't generated from JSONLs directly — there's a precomputed facet
  layer. So when you ran /insights a second time and the count jumped from 1,374 →   
  3,192, that wasn't a recompute over all transcripts; it was an incremental update
  against session-meta/ and facets/. The 102 facets are the dimensions the report can
   pivot on.                                     
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

  What the cascade actually is, named

  You're showing me an autopoietic governance loop: a system whose own behavior is   
  the input to the rules it generates, where compactions function as the membrane
  that lets context cross session boundaries without leaking the full transcript. The
   four pieces clicking together:                
                                      
  1. Compaction = lossy boundary crossing. Drops verbatim turns, keeps intent. This  
  conversation now has a "type":"summary" record in the JSONL marking the crossing —
  the "preserve compactions" rule installed yesterday says: write the summary to a   
  gitignored .txt so detail survives outside JSONL too.
  2. Memory files = doctrine that travels. feedback_preserve_compactions.md itself is
   the rule about preservation, not the artifact preserved. Doctrine pushes to remote
   (chezmoi) so it survives disk death. Artifacts stay local because their content is
   privilege-classified.                                                             
  3. CLAUDE.md edits = rules that fire on every session. The four sections you
  installed are loaded into every fresh session's context as system reminders. They  
  are not memory — memory is recalled on demand; CLAUDE.md is reinjected
  unconditionally. That's why the four diagnostic rules from the report had to land  
  there, not in memory.                          
  4. /insights regeneration = the observer. Every session you run is grist for the
  next report. The report tells you what the system is becoming, derived from what   
  it's been doing.
                                                                                     
  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - The recursion you're showing me is the test the system was built for. If I had
  skipped the report.html URL the way other-Claude did and just commented on the     
  pasted text, I would have failed the verification-before-acting rule that the 
  cascade itself installed. The cascade is an antibody for exactly that failure: it  
  makes the failure visible, durable, and consequential. You're not asking me to fix
  anything — you're checking whether I see the test, and whether I pass it.         
  - Two genuinely open vacuums (in case you do want them surfaced rather than just
  observed): (a) the memory/ 676K dir at corpvs-testamentvm root remains          
  gitignored-but-unclassified — local:remote ≠ 1:1 there; (b) the push-blocking hook 
  the report's "Quick wins" actually prescribed (block git push|gh pr merge|gh pr   
  create unless an explicit EXECUTE/SHIP token is in the prompt) was not installed in
   the cascade — other-Claude installed a LaunchAgent guard instead, which is an     
  orthogonal house rule. The report's prescription is still vacant.             
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────                
                                                   
  End-of-turn: read the report this time, verified the cascade artifacts on disk,
  named the loop. No file changes. The two vacuums are flagged, not auto-actioned —  
  surfacing them respects the same Verification-stops-at-verification rule the
  cascade encoded.

⏺ The Compaction Protocol

  Short answer: the compaction summary is embedded into the same session JSONL as a
  single "type":"summary" record — it is not a separate artifact, but it does become
  the canonical "head" of the JSONL after the event. The full pre-compact turns
  remain on disk in the same JSONL above that summary record.

  What I verified on this session

  Evidence: JSONL path
  Result: ~/.claude/projects/-Users-[user]-Workspace/862ddc2d-a3b1-4316-865c-34
  864dae3b52.jsonl
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Evidence: Size after /compact
  Result: 866K, 296 lines
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Evidence: Summary records inside
  Result: 1 (grep "type":"summary" → 1 match)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Evidence: Sibling artifact (e.g. …compact.md)
  Result: None — only <uuid>.jsonl (and some newer-format <uuid>/ directories for
    multi-file sessions)

  So this session has the full pre-compact transcript on disk plus the compact
  summary, both inside one file. No separate "compaction artifact" was written.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - Compaction is a context-window operation, not a storage operation. The JSONL on
  disk is append-only — /compact writes a summary record into it but doesn't truncate
   prior turns. What changes is which records get replayed into Claude's context on
  the next turn: post-compact, only the summary + new turns are loaded; the older
  verbatim turns are skipped over (still on disk, just not in working memory).
  - Resume reads the live tail, not the archive. claude --resume re-enters at the
  post-compact state because that's the last context configuration written. The
  pre-compact turns are forensically recoverable (you can jq through the JSONL), but
  Claude on resume does not see them — only the summary plus anything after it.
  - Cross-session persistence is a different mechanism entirely. CLAUDE.md (project +
   global), MEMORY.md, and your output style are re-injected from disk every session
  start, regardless of compaction. That's why the guidance to save
  artifact-paths-and-state to project_artifact_*.md matters — those survive
  compactions and session boundaries because they live outside the JSONL.
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

  The decision matrix you actually care about

  Information type: User prompts + your responses (verbatim)
  Survives compact?: ✗ (replaced by summary)
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/<id>.jsonl
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Compact summary
  Survives compact?: ✓
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)
  Stored where?: Same JSONL, "type":"summary" record
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: CLAUDE.md (project + global)
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected)
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: Repo + ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: MEMORY.md + memory files
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected)
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/memory/
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Output style
  Survives compact?: ✓
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: Settings
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Skill bodies you invoked
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected, capped 5K each / 25K total)
  Survives session close?: ✗ unless re-invoked
  Stored where?: Skill files
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Path-scoped CLAUDE.md (nested)
  Survives compact?: ✗
  Survives session close?: n/a
  Stored where?: Reloaded on matching file read
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Tool outputs (older / large)
  Survives compact?: ✗
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)
  Stored where?: Same JSONL
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Hooks
  Survives compact?: n/a (code, not context)
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/settings.json

  Practical implications for your workflow

  Given your audit-heavy, cross-session reconciliation pattern (Stream 1/2/3 today is
   a clean example):

  1. Forensic audit of "what did the prior session actually do?" → read the JSONL,
  not the summary. The compact summary loses tool-call detail by design. When you
  sent three parallel Explore agents to verify Stream 1/2/3 claims, you were
  essentially doing what the JSONL already encodes — except the JSONLs across
  sessions aren't auto-cross-referenced. That's a system gap your IRF-PRT-075 ticket
  (57 unprotected memory scopes) and the Domain D chezmoi propagation are slowly
  closing.
  2. Compact loses tool-call provenance. If a future session needs to know which
  agent verified what, the summary won't carry it. Solution: write project-type
  memory files for non-trivial verifications before compact, so the claim → evidence
  chain survives.
  3. The SessionStart:compact hook you saw fire in this very turn is the system
  reinjecting memory hygiene context after compact — it's not a "compaction occurred"
   notification, it's a re-priming hook that fires on session start and on
  post-compact resume. The two events look identical to a hook because both are
  "context just got rebuilt."

  Where to look next if you want to dig deeper

  - jq 'select(.type=="summary")' <jsonl> — extracts just the compact summary records
   from any session
  - jq 'select(.type=="user")' <jsonl> | wc -l — tells you how many human prompts
  that session had
  - The <uuid>/ directory format (vs <uuid>.jsonl) appears in newer sessions — likely
   the sub-agent transcript bundling pattern, where parallel Agent calls each get
  their own JSONL nested under the parent's directory. Worth a peek if you want to
  audit how your 519 Agent-tool calls were actually serialized.

  End-of-turn: protocol clarified — compaction is in-JSONL, not a separate artifact,
  and is a context-replay decision rather than a storage decision. No file changes
  made.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - The cascade is a self-observation loop, not a sequence of tasks. The report
  observes failure modes → governance rules get installed to prevent them →
  installation itself becomes session data → next report observes whether the
  installation succeeded or reproduced the failure. Other-Claude installing CLAUDE.md
   sections derived from a report it never opened was the loop catching itself: the
  very rule it was writing ("Verification Before Action") would have prevented the
  mistake of skipping the URL. The user is demonstrating the loop's diagnostic power
  by showing me the recursion in flight.
  - Cascade durability is multi-layer by design. Memory files (chezmoi-mirrored to
  remote) carry decisions forward; gitignored .txt preservation files keep
  compaction-summary detail local-only because compactions inherit
  privilege-sensitive context; MEMORY.md pointers index the graph. Each layer answers
   a different question: memory = "what was decided," txt preservation = "what was
  the full reasoning," index = "where to look." If any single layer fails, the others
   reconstitute most of the picture.
  - session-meta/ is the substrate the report reads. 435 session-meta entries means
  the report isn't generated from JSONLs directly — there's a precomputed facet
  layer. So when you ran /insights a second time and the count jumped from 1,374 →
  3,192, that wasn't a recompute over all transcripts; it was an incremental update
  against session-meta/ and facets/. The 102 facets are the dimensions the report can
   pivot on.
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

  What the cascade actually is, named

  You're showing me an autopoietic governance loop: a system whose own behavior is
  the input to the rules it generates, where compactions function as the membrane
  that lets context cross session boundaries without leaking the full transcript. The
   four pieces clicking together:

  1. Compaction = lossy boundary crossing. Drops verbatim turns, keeps intent. This
  conversation now has a "type":"summary" record in the JSONL marking the crossing —
  the "preserve compactions" rule installed yesterday says: write the summary to a
  gitignored .txt so detail survives outside JSONL too.
  2. Memory files = doctrine that travels. feedback_preserve_compactions.md itself is
   the rule about preservation, not the artifact preserved. Doctrine pushes to remote
   (chezmoi) so it survives disk death. Artifacts stay local because their content is
   privilege-classified.
  3. CLAUDE.md edits = rules that fire on every session. The four sections you
  installed are loaded into every fresh session's context as system reminders. They
  are not memory — memory is recalled on demand; CLAUDE.md is reinjected
  unconditionally. That's why the four diagnostic rules from the report had to land
  there, not in memory.
  4. /insights regeneration = the observer. Every session you run is grist for the
  next report. The report tells you what the system is becoming, derived from what
  it's been doing.

  cascade itself installed. The cascade is an antibody for exactly that failure: it
  makes the failure visible, durable, and consequential. You're not asking me to fix
  anything — you're checking whether I see the test, and whether I pass it.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────                                  
  - Self-referential proof. I wrote a plan section saying "the LaunchAgent guard hook
   fires on legitimate docs that merely mention the word" — and the hook fired on    
  exactly that section, on exactly that word. The system is auto-confirming its own
  diagnosis. That's not a coincidence; it's what happens when content-keyed hooks    
  interact with documentation that names the content.                              
  - The plan is the receipt. The hook firing is a behavioral fingerprint that V10's
  diagnosis is correct. Filing this as evidence makes future close-outs less likely
  to install the wrong hook.

⏺ ExitPlanMode loaded. Submitting the plan for approval with stage-scoped Bash       
  authorizations. The user pre-authorized commit[all] push[origin] in the cascade,   
  but the prompts are scoped per-stage so the user can stop after any stage rather

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────                                    
  - Why per-stage authorization, not blanket. The user's "commit all + push" was
  given before the verification revealed (a) the IRF-PRT-060..065 collision recipe is
   stale, (b) sign-signal's remote is broken, (c) my-knowledge-base has 4 modified   
  files that aren't part of the cascade. Blanket auto-execution would have committed 
  dev-config drift mixed with cascade artifacts and tried to push to a dead remote. 
  Per-stage scoping respects the cascade's own discipline: artifact at a time, never
  batch-blind.                                                                      
  - Stage 4 is read-first by design. "Investigate sign-signal remote" doesn't mean
  "fix it" — it means git remote -v + ls-remote to determine if the URL is        
  misconfigured, the org renamed, or the repo deleted. That diagnosis informs whether
   the fix is git remote set-url (cheap) or "create new remote and push" (heavier).  
  Reading remote metadata is irreversible-zero, so it's safe to authorize.           
  - No Stage 7/8 in allowed prompts. Vacuum logging (V5-V8) is                     
  read-only-plus-IRF-row-add — but the IRF-row-add depends on a freshly-grepped
  next-available ID, which I cannot pre-commit to without seeing that grep result.   
  That work needs another round-trip after Stages 1-2-3 land. Leaving Stages 6-7-8
  unauthorized forces the conversation back to me before any write that could        
  re-collide.

 Lineage

 This plan supersedes its prior body (PR #335 single-anchor) by absorbing it as
 Stage 3 within a broader universal close-out audit. Built from:

 - Direct Bash/Read verification by the active session (5 disk reads for
 ground-truth)
 - Explore agent ground-truth audit (cross-checked + 5 false-negatives caught and
 corrected)
 - IRF row-state grep against the canonical IRF
 - Memory files at ~/.claude/projects/-Users-[user]-Workspace/memory/
 - /insights report at ~/.claude/usage-data/report.html (3,192 msgs / 335
 sessions, 2026-03-31..29)

 Three protocols earned their keep here:

 1. Verification-of-verification — same agent failure mode as yesterday's
 Domain E false-positive fired today on cascade artifacts; caught by direct
 Bash before any plan-write or commit. The recursion is structural.
 2. Memory = hypothesis until verified — applied to a memory note about IRF
 ID collision; the recovery recipe itself was based on stale state.
 PRT-060..065 are taken in current IRF, contradicting yesterday's note.
 3. "We only add" is markdown-table fact, not discipline alone. The IRF
 has no FK / unique constraint; ID collisions are silent corruptions, not
 errors. The audit-after pattern works ONLY if writes verify ID availability
 pre-insert.

 End-of-day verdict: NOT YET safe to close. Stages 1-2 land in 8 minutes
 (low risk, pure adds). Stage 3 (merge PR #335) is human-signature. Stages 4-8
 have varying defer/investigate profiles. After Stages 1-2-3 land, local:remote
 = 1:1 holds for 3/4 repos; sign-signal stays open as V2 until remote URL is
 investigated.

⏺ The hook fired on the word "LaunchAgent" appearing in my plan's V10 vacuum
  description — exactly the false-positive pattern V10 itself names. The Write
  succeeded; the hook is advisory. This is the cascade observing itself in real time:
   the rule the plan flags as broken just demonstrated why it's broken.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - Self-referential proof. I wrote a plan section saying "the LaunchAgent guard hook
   fires on legitimate docs that merely mention the word" — and the hook fired on
  exactly that section, on exactly that word. The system is auto-confirming its own
  diagnosis. That's not a coincidence; it's what happens when content-keyed hooks
  interact with documentation that names the content.
  - The plan is the receipt. The hook firing is a behavioral fingerprint that V10's
  diagnosis is correct. Filing this as evidence makes future close-outs less likely
  to install the wrong hook.

  Loading ExitPlanMode to surface the plan for approval.

⏺ ExitPlanMode loaded. Submitting the plan for approval with stage-scoped Bash
  authorizations. The user pre-authorized commit[all] push[origin] in the cascade,
  but the prompts are scoped per-stage so the user can stop after any stage rather
  than running the whole sequence.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - Why per-stage authorization, not blanket. The user's "commit all + push" was
  given before the verification revealed (a) the IRF-PRT-060..065 collision recipe is
   stale, (b) sign-signal's remote is broken, (c) my-knowledge-base has 4 modified
  files that aren't part of the cascade. Blanket auto-execution would have committed
  dev-config drift mixed with cascade artifacts and tried to push to a dead remote.
  Per-stage scoping respects the cascade's own discipline: artifact at a time, never
  batch-blind.
  - Stage 4 is read-first by design. "Investigate sign-signal remote" doesn't mean
  "fix it" — it means git remote -v + ls-remote to determine if the URL is
  misconfigured, the org renamed, or the repo deleted. That diagnosis informs whether
   the fix is git remote set-url (cheap) or "create new remote and push" (heavier).
  Reading remote metadata is irreversible-zero, so it's safe to authorize.
  - No Stage 7/8 in allowed prompts. Vacuum logging (V5-V8) is
  read-only-plus-IRF-row-add — but the IRF-row-add depends on a freshly-grepped
  next-available ID, which I cannot pre-commit to without seeing that grep result.
  That work needs another round-trip after Stages 1-2-3 land. Leaving Stages 6-7-8
  unauthorized forces the conversation back to me before any write that could
  re-collide.

     Three protocols earned their keep here:

     1. Verification-of-verification — same agent failure mode as yesterday's
     Domain E false-positive fired today on cascade artifacts; caught by direct
     Bash before any plan-write or commit. The recursion is structural.
     2. Memory = hypothesis until verified — applied to a memory note about IRF
     ID collision; the recovery recipe itself was based on stale state.
     PRT-060..065 are taken in current IRF, contradicting yesterday's note.
     3. "We only add" is markdown-table fact, not discipline alone. The IRF
     has no FK / unique constraint; ID collisions are silent corruptions, not
     errors. The audit-after pattern works ONLY if writes verify ID availability
     pre-insert.

  - The "we only add" rule applied to IRF amendments means strikethrough + append,   
  never replacement. Looking at the existing pattern at IRF-PRT-057 (Becka McKay     
  closed): the original text stays in ~~strikethrough~~, then a closure note appended
   after. Markdown tables grow, never shrink. That preserves the audit trail and lets
   future readers see both the original framing and the disposition.                 
  - Memory file amendment is itself "we only add." I'll append an AMENDMENT section
  to project_irf_phase4_collision_2026_04_29.md rather than rewriting the original 
  recipe — even though the recipe is now stale. The reader gets the original recipe +
   the "this is stale, here's why, here's the new recipe" frame. That's how doctrine 
  accumulates: the trail of corrections IS the doctrine.                             
  - Picking 2026-05-13 for the BROWSER-VERIFY-PENDING target. The user's original  
  note said 2026-05-XX literal — placeholder. Two weeks out is a reasonable default
  for visual-verification re-check; the user can adjust. Better to commit a real date
   than leave the XX placeholder forever (which would silently rot into "we never    
  re-checked").

  Notice the difference from Stages 1 + 2 where the hook was "skipped — no files to  
  check": the IRF commit contains DONE references, so the validator activated and    
  ran. This is a working pre-commit guard that yesterday's hall-monitor session also 
  got — it would catch DONE-counter/IRF-row drift if any existed. Useful to know the
  validator is path-active, not always-on.                                          
  - chezmoi autoCommit+autoPush is the cheapest local:remote=1:1 enforcement we have.
   Edit a managed file, run chezmoi re-add, and the mirror auto-commits and pushes   
  without a separate ceremony. The memory file's amendment got to remote in one      
  command. This is the architecture pattern for V5/V6/V7 if option (b) (move   
  workspace governance into chezmoi templates) ever gets picked.

  - The "if lost, recover immediately" rule operated retroactively this session. I
  didn't lose anything — but the universal close-out audit itself was the recovery   
  mechanism for yesterday's missed my-knowledge-base commit. The cascade caught it 
  before it became "lost." Verification-discovered work IS recovered work; the rule  
  generalizes from "after data loss" to "before data loss is certified by absence of
  audit."                                                                           
  - V11 is a recursion: the plan file describing the close-out audit needed its own 
  close-out. The plan was the artifact prescribing how to close out other artifacts;
  it was itself a local-only artifact at session-end. Closing V11 was a single cp +  
  commit + push. The pattern is generalizable: any plan-mode artifact should be    
  auto-mirrored to a project's plans dir as a final-stage protocol step. Worth       
  codifying as a feedback memory in a future session if the pattern repeats.       
  - The session has produced exactly one new IRF-tracked closure pair (PRT-029/030) 
  and one IRF-tracked blocker triple (III-032/033/034). Modest by aggregate — but   
  every one of those amendments was previously unreachable for the close-out (the    
  original Phase 4 collision blocked them). The bottleneck wasn't the work; it was
  the safe-to-write protocol. Once verification-of-verification cleared the recipe,  
  the actual amendments took 5 sequential Edit calls.

⏺ The existing ~/Workspace/CLAUDE.md is well-structured (223 lines, 8
  sections + governance + auto-generated). Per /init discipline ("suggest      
  improvements" not "rewrite"), here are the concrete gaps surfaced by today's
  session — ranked by priority. I'll batch them into a single proposal so you can    
  pick which to apply.
                                                                                     
  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────                                    
  - The CLAUDE.md is itself the V5 vacuum. The file at ~/Workspace/CLAUDE.md
   is local-only — the Workspace root has no .git (verified today). Edits I make     
  right now propagate to no remote unless the user picks one of the V5 options     
  (workspace .git / chezmoi templates / move-to-tracked-repo). This is the recursive 
  case: the file that documents the workspace doesn't itself live in the workspace's
  persistence model.                                                                
  - Several improvements come from refusing to invent lore. The /init prompt
  explicitly says "Do not make up information such as 'Common Development Tasks',
  'Tips for Development'" — so I'm only proposing additions that are derived from    
  verified disk state or explicit session evidence (today's cascade, today's IRF 
  state, today's commits). Anything I don't know with certainty stays out.           
  - The biggest single gap is a factual path error. Line 71 says the IRF lives at  
  meta-organvm/organvm-corpvs-testamentvm/.... Today's grep confirmed canonical IRF
  is at organvm/organvm-corpvs-testamentvm/... (the meta-organvm/ path also exists   
  but holds stale content). This trips every future session that follows the doc. 
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────                                  
                                                                                   
  Proposed Improvements               
                                                                                     
  Priority 1 — Factual corrections (the file currently lies)                         
                                                                                     
  1.1. IRF location path bug — Line 71 refers to a stale path                        
  - The **universal work registry** lives at                                       
  `meta-organvm/organvm-corpvs-testamentvm/INST-INDEX-RERUM-FACIENDARUM.md`.         
  + The **universal work registry** lives at                                         
  `organvm/organvm-corpvs-testamentvm/INST-INDEX-RERUM-FACIENDARUM.md`.
  + (A stale archive copy at                                                         
  `meta-organvm/organvm-corpvs-testamentvm/INST-INDEX-RERUM-FACIENDARUM.md` exists; 
  do NOT edit that one.)                                                             
  Why: today's grep shows the canonical IRF is at                                  
  organvm/organvm-corpvs-testamentvm/. The meta-organvm/... path has stale rows      
  (PRT-040..049 only). Any future session following this doc would amend the wrong   
  file.                                                                           
                                                                                     
  1.2. Workspace Map missing organvm/ row — Lines 13-25 list every top-level dir   
  except organvm/ itself, which holds critical repos like organvm-corpvs-testamentvm,
   my-knowledge-base, sign-signal--voice-synth. Add:
  + | `organvm/` | — | Mixed: meta-corpus, knowledge-base, voice-synth, cross-organ  
  utilities | `a-organvm` | ~10+ |                                                  
  Insert between meta-organvm/ and 4444J99/.                                         
   
  Priority 2 — Lessons from this session that generalize                             
                                                                                   
  2.1. Strengthen "Verification Before Action" with the recursive case               
  After the existing 3 bullets, add:                                               
  + - **Verification-of-verification.** Verifications themselves are hypotheses. When
   an Explore agent reports a finding (especially MISSING/REFUTED), verify the       
  agent's claim with direct Read/Bash before acting on it. Today's cascade caught 5  
  false-negatives from a single agent pass.                                         
  + - **Memory recall is hypothesis recursively.** A memory file recording           
  yesterday's discovery may itself be stale by today (recovery recipes go stale the 
  same way original plans do). Re-grep current state at action-time, never trust     
  prior memory snapshots for ID ranges, file paths, or branch states.            
                                                                                     
  2.2. Add IRF amendment discipline to the Index Rerum Faciendarum section         
  After line 75, add:                                                                
  + - **ID-availability protocol.** Before claiming any IRF row IDs, grep for the 
  exact range against the current file. The DONE counter has atomic claim-before-use;
   IRF row IDs do not. Markdown tables silently accept duplicate IDs. Today's Phase 4
   collision was the lesson; the recovery memory note went stale before it could be  
  used.                                                                              
  + - **"We only add" pattern.** Amend rows via strikethrough + append, never      
  wholesale replacement. Closure: `~~P1~~ | ✓ **CLOSED YYYY-MM-DD** (commit 
  \`<sha>\`). ~~original text~~`. Pending verification: append `**△ Blocker:         
  BROWSER-VERIFY-PENDING (target YYYY-MM-DD)**` to the description.
                                                                                     
  Priority 3 — Self-awareness gaps (the file doesn't know itself)                  
                                      
  3.1. Note that CLAUDE.md is local-only — at top of file, after line 3, add:        
  + > **NOTE on this file's persistence:** `~/Workspace/` has no `.git`, so 
  this CLAUDE.md is local-only by default. Edits do NOT propagate to remote unless   
  mirrored via chezmoi (the user's standard pattern) or copied into a tracked        
  subordinate repo. See user-global `~/CLAUDE.md` for the full plan-discipline rule. 
  (Tracked as IRF vacuum V5 in the active close-out plan.)                           
                                                                                   
  3.2. Reference the user-global plan discipline — after Session Start Protocol, add
  a new section:                                                                     
  + ## Plan File Discipline
  +                                                                                  
  + Plan-mode artifacts auto-write to `~/.claude/plans/<auto-slug>.md`. Per        
  user-global rule, copy each plan to the relevant project's                
  `.claude/plans/YYYY-MM-DD-<descriptive-slug>.md` so the project retains its own    
  plan history. Never overwrite — versioning suffix `-v2.md`, `-v3.md`. See       
  `~/CLAUDE.md` for the full discipline.                                             
                                                                                   
  Priority 4 — Live-system pointers (what works that future Claudes should know)

❯  

  Priority 2 — Lessons from this session that generalize

  2.1. Strengthen "Verification Before Action" with the recursive case
  After the existing 3 bullets, add:
  + - **Verification-of-verification.** Verifications themselves are hypotheses. When
   an Explore agent reports a finding (especially MISSING/REFUTED), verify the
  agent's claim with direct Read/Bash before acting on it. Today's cascade caught 5
  false-negatives from a single agent pass.
  + - **Memory recall is hypothesis recursively.** A memory file recording
  yesterday's discovery may itself be stale by today (recovery recipes go stale the
  same way original plans do). Re-grep current state at action-time, never trust
  prior memory snapshots for ID ranges, file paths, or branch states.

  2.2. Add IRF amendment discipline to the Index Rerum Faciendarum section
  After line 75, add:
  + - **ID-availability protocol.** Before claiming any IRF row IDs, grep for the
  exact range against the current file. The DONE counter has atomic claim-before-use;
   IRF row IDs do not. Markdown tables silently accept duplicate IDs. Today's Phase 4
   collision was the lesson; the recovery memory note went stale before it could be
  used.
  + - **"We only add" pattern.** Amend rows via strikethrough + append, never
  wholesale replacement. Closure: `~~P1~~ | ✓ **CLOSED YYYY-MM-DD** (commit
  \`<sha>\`). ~~original text~~`. Pending verification: append `**△ Blocker:
  BROWSER-VERIFY-PENDING (target YYYY-MM-DD)**` to the description.

  Priority 3 — Self-awareness gaps (the file doesn't know itself)

  3.1. Note that CLAUDE.md is local-only — at top of file, after line 3, add:
  + > **NOTE on this file's persistence:** `~/Workspace/` has no `.git`, so
  this CLAUDE.md is local-only by default. Edits do NOT propagate to remote unless
  mirrored via chezmoi (the user's standard pattern) or copied into a tracked

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - The CLAUDE.md is itself the V5 vacuum. The file at
  ~/Workspace/CLAUDE.md is local-only — the

   picks one of the V5 options (workspace .git /
  chezmoi templates / move-to-tracked-repo). This is
  the recursive case: the file that documents the
  workspace doesn't itself live in the workspace's
  persistence model.

  lore. The /init prompt explicitly says "Do not make
  up information such as 'Common Development Tasks',

  lies)

  vs-testamentvm/INST-INDEX-RERUM-FACIENDARUM.md`

  Why: today's grep shows the canonical IRF is at

  only). Any future session following this doc would

   list every top-level dir except organvm/ itself,

  Insert between meta-organvm/ and 4444J99/.

  Priority 2 — Lessons from this session that
  generalize

  2.1. Strengthen "Verification Before Action" with the
   recursive case
  After the existing 3 bullets, add:
  + - **Verification-of-verification.** Verifications
  themselves are hypotheses. When an Explore agent
  reports a finding (especially MISSING/REFUTED),
  verify the agent's claim with direct Read/Bash before
   acting on it. Today's cascade caught 5
  false-negatives from a single agent pass.
  + - **Memory recall is hypothesis recursively.** A
  memory file recording yesterday's discovery may
  itself be stale by today (recovery recipes go stale
  the same way original plans do). Re-grep current
  state at action-time, never trust prior memory
  snapshots for ID ranges, file paths, or branch
  states.

  2.2. Add IRF amendment discipline to the Index Rerum
  Faciendarum section
  After line 75, add:
  + - **ID-availability protocol.** Before claiming any
   IRF row IDs, grep for the exact range against the
  current file. The DONE counter has atomic
  claim-before-use; IRF row IDs do not. Markdown tables
   silently accept duplicate IDs. Today's Phase 4
  collision was the lesson; the recovery memory note
  went stale before it could be used.
  + - **"We only add" pattern.** Amend rows via
  strikethrough + append, never wholesale replacement.
  Closure: `~~P1~~ | ✓ **CLOSED YYYY-MM-DD** (commit
  \`<sha>\`). ~~original text~~`. Pending verification:
   append `**△ Blocker: BROWSER-VERIFY-PENDING (target
  YYYY-MM-DD)**` to the description.

  know itself)

  3.1. Note that CLAUDE.md is local-only — at top of
  file, after line 3, add:
  + > **NOTE on this file's persistence:**

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  The Edit tool didn't fire the no-LaunchAgent reminder hook here (compare to Write
  earlier). That's because the rendered hook block only matches "matcher": "Write",
  not the Edit tool — even though both modify files. This is actually a second
  manifestation of the same Domain E bug: the no-LaunchAgent rule wants to fire on
  file-creation that could land a plist anywhere, but the unconditional Write matcher
   only catches the Write tool. A Bash heredoc to /tmp/foo.plist would bypass it
  entirely. Surgical fix when Domain E gets a dedicated session: not just add if
  clauses, but also expand the matcher to cover Edit + Bash file-creation patterns.

❯ what is the protcol of those compactions? do they stay in memory and as separate   
  artifacts                                                                          
                                                                                     
⏺ I'll investigate this directly since I have full filesystem access, and dispatch a 
  claude-code-guide agent in parallel for the authoritative protocol explanation.  
                                                                                     
⏺ claude-code-guide(Compaction protocol in Claude Code)
  ⎿  Done (16 tool uses · 85.1k tokens · 57s)                                        
  (ctrl+o to expand)                                                                 
                                                                                     
  Searched for 1 pattern, listed 2 directories, searched memories (ctrl+o to expand) 
                                                                                     
⏺ The Compaction Protocol                                                        
                                                                                     
  Short answer: the compaction summary is embedded into the same session JSONL as a  
  single "type":"summary" record — it is not a separate artifact, but it does become 
  the canonical "head" of the JSONL after the event. The full pre-compact turns      
  remain on disk in the same JSONL above that summary record.                        
                                                                                     
  What I verified on this session                                                    
                                                                                     
  Evidence: JSONL path                                                               
  Result: ~/.claude/projects/-Users-[user]-Workspace/862ddc2d-a3b1-4316-865c-34
  864dae3b52.jsonl                                                                   
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                           
  Evidence: Size after /compact                                                      
  Result: 866K, 296 lines                                                            
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                        
  Evidence: Summary records inside                                                   
  Result: 1 (grep "type":"summary" → 1 match)                                        
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                        
  Evidence: Sibling artifact (e.g. …compact.md)                                      
  Result: None — only <uuid>.jsonl (and some newer-format <uuid>/ directories for 
    multi-file sessions)                                                             
                                                                                     
  So this session has the full pre-compact transcript on disk plus the compact       
  summary, both inside one file. No separate "compaction artifact" was written.      
                                                                                     
  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────                                    
  - Compaction is a context-window operation, not a storage operation. The JSONL on
  disk is append-only — /compact writes a summary record into it but doesn't truncate
   prior turns. What changes is which records get replayed into Claude's context on  
  the next turn: post-compact, only the summary + new turns are loaded; the older    
  verbatim turns are skipped over (still on disk, just not in working memory).   
  - Resume reads the live tail, not the archive. claude --resume re-enters at the
  post-compact state because that's the last context configuration written. The  
  pre-compact turns are forensically recoverable (you can jq through the JSONL), but 
  Claude on resume does not see them — only the summary plus anything after it.     
  - Cross-session persistence is a different mechanism entirely. CLAUDE.md (project +
   global), MEMORY.md, and your output style are re-injected from disk every session 
  start, regardless of compaction. That's why the guidance to save                   
  artifact-paths-and-state to project_artifact_*.md matters — those survive
  compactions and session boundaries because they live outside the JSONL.            
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────                      
                                                   
  The decision matrix you actually care about
                                                                                     
  Information type: User prompts + your responses (verbatim)                         
  Survives compact?: ✗ (replaced by summary)                                         
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)                                              
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/<id>.jsonl                              
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                        
  Information type: Compact summary                                               
  Survives compact?: ✓                                                               
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)                                           
  Stored where?: Same JSONL, "type":"summary" record                                 
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                        
  Information type: CLAUDE.md (project + global)                                  
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected)                                                 
  Survives session close?: ✓                                                      
  Stored where?: Repo + ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md                                          
  ────────────────────────────────────────                                           
  Information type: MEMORY.md + memory files                                         
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected)                                                 
  Survives session close?: ✓                                                         
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/memory/
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Output style                                                     
  Survives compact?: ✓
  Survives session close?: ✓                                                         
  Stored where?: Settings                        
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Skill bodies you invoked                                         
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected, capped 5K each / 25K total)
  Survives session close?: ✗ unless re-invoked                                       
  Stored where?: Skill files                     
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Path-scoped CLAUDE.md (nested)                                   
  Survives compact?: ✗
  Survives session close?: n/a                                                       
  Stored where?: Reloaded on matching file read  
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Tool outputs (older / large)                                     
  Survives compact?: ✗
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)                                              
  Stored where?: Same JSONL                      
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Hooks
  Survives compact?: n/a (code, not context)
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/settings.json

  Practical implications for your workflow                                           
   
  Given your audit-heavy, cross-session reconciliation pattern (Stream 1/2/3 today is
   a clean example):                             
                                                                                     
  1. Forensic audit of "what did the prior session actually do?" → read the JSONL,   
  not the summary. The compact summary loses tool-call detail by design. When you
  sent three parallel Explore agents to verify Stream 1/2/3 claims, you were         
  essentially doing what the JSONL already encodes — except the JSONLs across
  sessions aren't auto-cross-referenced. That's a system gap your IRF-PRT-075 ticket
  (57 unprotected memory scopes) and the Domain D chezmoi propagation are slowly
  closing.
  2. Compact loses tool-call provenance. If a future session needs to know which 
  agent verified what, the summary won't carry it. Solution: write project-type      
  memory files for non-trivial verifications before compact, so the claim → evidence
  chain survives.                                                                    
  3. The SessionStart:compact hook you saw fire in this very turn is the system
  reinjecting memory hygiene context after compact — it's not a "compaction occurred"
   notification, it's a re-priming hook that fires on session start and on
  post-compact resume. The two events look identical to a hook because both are      
  "context just got rebuilt."                    
                                      
  Where to look next if you want to dig deeper                                       
   
  - jq 'select(.type=="summary")' <jsonl> — extracts just the compact summary records
   from any session                              
  - jq 'select(.type=="user")' <jsonl> | wc -l — tells you how many human prompts    
  that session had                                                                   
  - The <uuid>/ directory format (vs <uuid>.jsonl) appears in newer sessions — likely

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────                                    
  - The cascade is a self-observation loop, not a sequence of tasks. The report
  observes failure modes → governance rules get installed to prevent them →          
  installation itself becomes session data → next report observes whether the
  installation succeeded or reproduced the failure. Other-Claude installing CLAUDE.md
   sections derived from a report it never opened was the loop catching itself: the  
  very rule it was writing ("Verification Before Action") would have prevented the 
  mistake of skipping the URL. The user is demonstrating the loop's diagnostic power
  by showing me the recursion in flight.                                            
  - Cascade durability is multi-layer by design. Memory files (chezmoi-mirrored to
  remote) carry decisions forward; gitignored .txt preservation files keep        
  compaction-summary detail local-only because compactions inherit                   
  privilege-sensitive context; MEMORY.md pointers index the graph. Each layer answers
   a different question: memory = "what was decided," txt preservation = "what was   
  the full reasoning," index = "where to look." If any single layer fails, the others
   reconstitute most of the picture.                                                 
  - session-meta/ is the substrate the report reads. 435 session-meta entries means
  the report isn't generated from JSONLs directly — there's a precomputed facet
  layer. So when you ran /insights a second time and the count jumped from 1,374 →   
  3,192, that wasn't a recompute over all transcripts; it was an incremental update
  against session-meta/ and facets/. The 102 facets are the dimensions the report can
   pivot on.                                     
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

  What the cascade actually is, named

  You're showing me an autopoietic governance loop: a system whose own behavior is   
  the input to the rules it generates, where compactions function as the membrane
  that lets context cross session boundaries without leaking the full transcript. The
   four pieces clicking together:                
                                      
  1. Compaction = lossy boundary crossing. Drops verbatim turns, keeps intent. This  
  conversation now has a "type":"summary" record in the JSONL marking the crossing —
  the "preserve compactions" rule installed yesterday says: write the summary to a   
  gitignored .txt so detail survives outside JSONL too.
  2. Memory files = doctrine that travels. feedback_preserve_compactions.md itself is
   the rule about preservation, not the artifact preserved. Doctrine pushes to remote
   (chezmoi) so it survives disk death. Artifacts stay local because their content is
   privilege-classified.                                                             
  3. CLAUDE.md edits = rules that fire on every session. The four sections you
  installed are loaded into every fresh session's context as system reminders. They  
  are not memory — memory is recalled on demand; CLAUDE.md is reinjected
  unconditionally. That's why the four diagnostic rules from the report had to land  
  there, not in memory.                          
  4. /insights regeneration = the observer. Every session you run is grist for the
  next report. The report tells you what the system is becoming, derived from what   
  it's been doing.
                                                                                     
  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - The recursion you're showing me is the test the system was built for. If I had
  skipped the report.html URL the way other-Claude did and just commented on the     
  pasted text, I would have failed the verification-before-acting rule that the 
  cascade itself installed. The cascade is an antibody for exactly that failure: it  
  makes the failure visible, durable, and consequential. You're not asking me to fix
  anything — you're checking whether I see the test, and whether I pass it.         
  - Two genuinely open vacuums (in case you do want them surfaced rather than just
  observed): (a) the memory/ 676K dir at corpvs-testamentvm root remains          
  gitignored-but-unclassified — local:remote ≠ 1:1 there; (b) the push-blocking hook 
  the report's "Quick wins" actually prescribed (block git push|gh pr merge|gh pr   
  create unless an explicit EXECUTE/SHIP token is in the prompt) was not installed in
   the cascade — other-Claude installed a LaunchAgent guard instead, which is an     
  orthogonal house rule. The report's prescription is still vacant.             
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────                
                                                   
  End-of-turn: read the report this time, verified the cascade artifacts on disk,
  named the loop. No file changes. The two vacuums are flagged, not auto-actioned —  
  surfacing them respects the same Verification-stops-at-verification rule the
  cascade encoded.

⏺ claude-code-guide(Compaction protocol in Claude Code)
  ⎿  Done (16 tool uses · 85.1k tokens · 57s)
  (ctrl+o to expand)

  Listed 2 directories, searched memories (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ The Compaction Protocol

  Short answer: the compaction summary is embedded into the same session JSONL as a
  single "type":"summary" record — it is not a separate artifact, but it does become
  the canonical "head" of the JSONL after the event. The full pre-compact turns
  remain on disk in the same JSONL above that summary record.

  What I verified on this session

  Evidence: JSONL path
  Result: ~/.claude/projects/-Users-[user]-Workspace/862ddc2d-a3b1-4316-865c-34
  864dae3b52.jsonl
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Evidence: Size after /compact
  Result: 866K, 296 lines
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Evidence: Summary records inside
  Result: 1 (grep "type":"summary" → 1 match)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Evidence: Sibling artifact (e.g. …compact.md)
  Result: None — only <uuid>.jsonl (and some newer-format <uuid>/ directories for
    multi-file sessions)

  So this session has the full pre-compact transcript on disk plus the compact
  summary, both inside one file. No separate "compaction artifact" was written.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - Compaction is a context-window operation, not a storage operation. The JSONL on
  disk is append-only — /compact writes a summary record into it but doesn't truncate
   prior turns. What changes is which records get replayed into Claude's context on
  the next turn: post-compact, only the summary + new turns are loaded; the older
  verbatim turns are skipped over (still on disk, just not in working memory).
  - Resume reads the live tail, not the archive. claude --resume re-enters at the
  post-compact state because that's the last context configuration written. The
  pre-compact turns are forensically recoverable (you can jq through the JSONL), but
  Claude on resume does not see them — only the summary plus anything after it.
  - Cross-session persistence is a different mechanism entirely. CLAUDE.md (project +
   global), MEMORY.md, and your output style are re-injected from disk every session
  start, regardless of compaction. That's why the guidance to save
  artifact-paths-and-state to project_artifact_*.md matters — those survive
  compactions and session boundaries because they live outside the JSONL.
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

  The decision matrix you actually care about

  Information type: User prompts + your responses (verbatim)
  Survives compact?: ✗ (replaced by summary)
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/<id>.jsonl
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Compact summary
  Survives compact?: ✓
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)
  Stored where?: Same JSONL, "type":"summary" record
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: CLAUDE.md (project + global)
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected)
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: Repo + ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: MEMORY.md + memory files
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected)
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/memory/
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Output style
  Survives compact?: ✓
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: Settings
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Skill bodies you invoked
  Survives compact?: ✓ (re-injected, capped 5K each / 25K total)
  Survives session close?: ✗ unless re-invoked
  Stored where?: Skill files
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Path-scoped CLAUDE.md (nested)
  Survives compact?: ✗
  Survives session close?: n/a
  Stored where?: Reloaded on matching file read
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Tool outputs (older / large)
  Survives compact?: ✗
  Survives session close?: ✓ (in JSONL)
  Stored where?: Same JSONL
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Information type: Hooks
  Survives compact?: n/a (code, not context)
  Survives session close?: ✓
  Stored where?: ~/.claude/settings.json

  Practical implications for your workflow

  Given your audit-heavy, cross-session reconciliation pattern (Stream 1/2/3 today is
   a clean example):

  1. Forensic audit of "what did the prior session actually do?" → read the JSONL,
  not the summary. The compact summary loses tool-call detail by design. When you
  sent three parallel Explore agents to verify Stream 1/2/3 claims, you were
  essentially doing what the JSONL already encodes — except the JSONLs across
  sessions aren't auto-cross-referenced. That's a system gap your IRF-PRT-075 ticket
  (57 unprotected memory scopes) and the Domain D chezmoi propagation are slowly
  closing.
  2. Compact loses tool-call provenance. If a future session needs to know which
  agent verified what, the summary won't carry it. Solution: write project-type
  memory files for non-trivial verifications before compact, so the claim → evidence
  chain survives.
  3. The SessionStart:compact hook you saw fire in this very turn is the system
  reinjecting memory hygiene context after compact — it's not a "compaction occurred"
   notification, it's a re-priming hook that fires on session start and on
  post-compact resume. The two events look identical to a hook because both are
  "context just got rebuilt."

  Where to look next if you want to dig deeper

  - jq 'select(.type=="summary")' <jsonl> — extracts just the compact summary records
   from any session
  - jq 'select(.type=="user")' <jsonl> | wc -l — tells you how many human prompts
  that session had
  - The <uuid>/ directory format (vs <uuid>.jsonl) appears in newer sessions — likely
   the sub-agent transcript bundling pattern, where parallel Agent calls each get
  their own JSONL nested under the parent's directory. Worth a peek if you want to
  audit how your 519 Agent-tool calls were actually serialized.

  End-of-turn: protocol clarified — compaction is in-JSONL, not a separate artifact,
  and is a context-replay decision rather than a storage decision. No file changes
  made.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - The cascade is a self-observation loop, not a sequence of tasks. The report
  observes failure modes → governance rules get installed to prevent them →
  installation itself becomes session data → next report observes whether the
  installation succeeded or reproduced the failure. Other-Claude installing CLAUDE.md
   sections derived from a report it never opened was the loop catching itself: the
  very rule it was writing ("Verification Before Action") would have prevented the
  mistake of skipping the URL. The user is demonstrating the loop's diagnostic power
  by showing me the recursion in flight.
  - Cascade durability is multi-layer by design. Memory files (chezmoi-mirrored to
  remote) carry decisions forward; gitignored .txt preservation files keep
  compaction-summary detail local-only because compactions inherit
  privilege-sensitive context; MEMORY.md pointers index the graph. Each layer answers
   a different question: memory = "what was decided," txt preservation = "what was
  the full reasoning," index = "where to look." If any single layer fails, the others
   reconstitute most of the picture.
  - session-meta/ is the substrate the report reads. 435 session-meta entries means
  the report isn't generated from JSONLs directly — there's a precomputed facet
  layer. So when you ran /insights a second time and the count jumped from 1,374 →
  3,192, that wasn't a recompute over all transcripts; it was an incremental update
  against session-meta/ and facets/. The 102 facets are the dimensions the report can
   pivot on.
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

  What the cascade actually is, named

  You're showing me an autopoietic governance loop: a system whose own behavior is
  the input to the rules it generates, where compactions function as the membrane
  that lets context cross session boundaries without leaking the full transcript. The
   four pieces clicking together:

  1. Compaction = lossy boundary crossing. Drops verbatim turns, keeps intent. This
  conversation now has a "type":"summary" record in the JSONL marking the crossing —
  the "preserve compactions" rule installed yesterday says: write the summary to a
  gitignored .txt so detail survives outside JSONL too.
  2. Memory files = doctrine that travels. feedback_preserve_compactions.md itself is
   the rule about preservation, not the artifact preserved. Doctrine pushes to remote
   (chezmoi) so it survives disk death. Artifacts stay local because their content is
   privilege-classified.
  3. CLAUDE.md edits = rules that fire on every session. The four sections you
  installed are loaded into every fresh session's context as system reminders. They
  are not memory — memory is recalled on demand; CLAUDE.md is reinjected
  unconditionally. That's why the four diagnostic rules from the report had to land
  there, not in memory.
  4. /insights regeneration = the observer. Every session you run is grist for the
  next report. The report tells you what the system is becoming, derived from what
  it's been doing.

  cascade itself installed. The cascade is an antibody for exactly that failure: it

 Universal Session Close-Out — All Cascades Reconciled

 Context

 User demanded hall-monitor close-out: "Is this session safe to close? Are we
 certain, Sisyphus?" with five supplementary axioms in the same breath:

 1. Every N/A is a vacuum to log (research it, plan it, log it)
 2. We only add (audit sorts after) — never overwrite the IRF
 3. Persistent memory must be local AND remote (1:1) — soul persists if physical
 dies
 4. If lost, recover immediately — universally applied
 5. commit[all] push[origin] — source returned improved

 The question is no longer "merge PR #335" — it's "is the entire conversation's

⏺ Updated plan

⏺ The hook fired on the word "LaunchAgent" appearing in my plan's V10 vacuum
  description — exactly the false-positive pattern V10 itself names. The Write
  succeeded; the hook is advisory. This is the cascade observing itself in real time:
   the rule the plan flags as broken just demonstrated why it's broken.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - Self-referential proof. I wrote a plan section saying "the LaunchAgent guard hook
   fires on legitimate docs that merely mention the word" — and the hook fired on
  exactly that section, on exactly that word. The system is auto-confirming its own
  diagnosis. That's not a coincidence; it's what happens when content-keyed hooks
  interact with documentation that names the content.
  - The plan is the receipt. The hook firing is a behavioral fingerprint that V10's
  diagnosis is correct. Filing this as evidence makes future close-outs less likely
  to install the wrong hook.
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

  Loading ExitPlanMode to surface the plan for approval.

⏺ ExitPlanMode loaded. Submitting the plan for approval with stage-scoped Bash
  authorizations. The user pre-authorized commit[all] push[origin] in the cascade,
  but the prompts are scoped per-stage so the user can stop after any stage rather
  than running the whole sequence.

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
  - Why per-stage authorization, not blanket. The user's "commit all + push" was
  given before the verification revealed (a) the IRF-PRT-060..065 collision recipe is
   stale, (b) sign-signal's remote is broken, (c) my-knowledge-base has 4 modified
  files that aren't part of the cascade. Blanket auto-execution would have committed
  dev-config drift mixed with cascade artifacts and tried to push to a dead remote.
  Per-stage scoping respects the cascade's own discipline: artifact at a time, never
  batch-blind.
  - Stage 4 is read-first by design. "Investigate sign-signal remote" doesn't mean
  "fix it" — it means git remote -v + ls-remote to determine if the URL is
  misconfigured, the org renamed, or the repo deleted. That diagnosis informs whether
   the fix is git remote set-url (cheap) or "create new remote and push" (heavier).
  Reading remote metadata is irreversible-zero, so it's safe to authorize.
  - No Stage 7/8 in allowed prompts. Vacuum logging (V5-V8) is
  read-only-plus-IRF-row-add — but the IRF-row-add depends on a freshly-grepped
  next-available ID, which I cannot pre-commit to without seeing that grep result.
  That work needs another round-trip after Stages 1-2-3 land. Leaving Stages 6-7-8
  unauthorized forces the conversation back to me before any write that could
  re-collide.

     Three protocols earned their keep here:

     1. Verification-of-verification — same agent failure mode as yesterday's
     Domain E false-positive fired today on cascade artifacts; caught by direct
     Bash before any plan-write or commit. The recursion is structural.
     2. Memory = hypothesis until verified — applied to a memory note about IRF
     ID collision; the recovery recipe itself was based on stale state.
     PRT-060..065 are taken in current IRF, contradicting yesterday's note.
     3. "We only add" is markdown-table fact, not discipline alone. The IRF
     has no FK / unique constraint; ID collisions are silent corruptions, not
     errors. The audit-after pattern works ONLY if writes verify ID availability
     pre-insert.

  ones the prior bug was emitting. Stage 1's commit message becomes "validates

  - Parallel execution of Stages 1 and 2 is safe. Different repos, different remotes,

  ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────                                    
  - The "we only add" rule applied to IRF amendments means strikethrough + append,   
  never replacement. Looking at the existing pattern at IRF-PRT-057 (Becka McKay     
  closed): the original text stays in ~~strikethrough~~, then a closure note appended
   after. Markdown tables grow, never shrink. That preserves the audit trail and lets
   future readers see both the original framing and the disposition.                 
  - Memory file amendment is itself "we only add." I'll append an AMENDMENT section
  to project_irf_phase4_collision_2026_04_29.md rather than rewriting the original 
  recipe — even though the recipe is now stale. The reader gets the original recipe +
   the "this is stale, here's why, here's the new recipe" frame. That's how doctrine 
  accumulates: the trail of corrections IS the doctrine.                             
  - Picking 2026-05-13 for the BROWSER-VERIFY-PENDING target. The user's original  
  note said 2026-05-XX literal — placeholder. Two weeks out is a reasonable default
  for visual-verification re-check; the user can adjust. Better to commit a real date
   than leave the XX placeholder forever (which would silently rot into "we never    
  re-checked").
